# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kafka Old Consumer API to New Consumer API Migration

## Your Task

Analyze the migration from the old Kafka consumer API (kafka.consumer.ConsumerConnector) to the new KafkaConsumer API in apache/kafka. Find Java source files that (1) implement the legacy ConsumerConnector interface, (2) implement the new KafkaConsumer API, and identify the key behavioral differences in offset management.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of the Kafka consumer API migration. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary

I've analyzed the migration from the legacy Kafka consumer API to the modern KafkaConsumer API across the Apache Kafka, Flink, and Camel repositories. Here are the key findings:

### Core Architecture
The current Kafka implementation uses a **delegation pattern** where `KafkaConsumer` (the public API) delegates to one of two implementations:
- **ClassicKafkaConsumer**: Legacy group protocol (pre-KIP 848) with synchronous architecture
- **AsyncKafkaConsumer**: New group protocol (KIP-848) with event-driven architecture

### Offset Management Differences

**Legacy (ClassicKafkaConsumer):**
- Uses `ConsumerCoordinator` for group coordination and offset commits
- Synchronous, blocking offset commit methods (`commitSync`, `commitAsync`)
- Direct API calls trigger immediate offset commit requests
- Manages offsets through `OffsetFetcher` and stored `OffsetAndMetadata`

**Modern (AsyncKafkaConsumer):**
- Uses dedicated `CommitRequestManager` for offset operations
- Event-based architecture with background threads handling commits
- Commits enqueued as `SyncCommitEvent` or `AsyncCommitEvent` for async processing
- CompletableFuture-based API instead of callbacks

### Integration Points
- **Camel**: Uses the Consumer interface with `SyncCommitManager` and `AsyncCommitManager` for offset management
- **Flink**: FlinkKafkaConsumer is deprecated, replaced by KafkaSource

The analysis includes 17 critical files and 12 key symbols documenting the complete migration architecture, saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

Modern Implementation\\n\\n### Overview\\nThe Apache Kafka codebase has evolved from a legacy `ConsumerConnector` interface to the modern `KafkaConsumer` API, which now supports multiple consumer group protocols (classic and new) through an internal delegation pattern.\\n\\n### Core Implementation Files\\n\\n#### Kafka Repository (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489)\\n\\n**New KafkaConsumer API Architecture:**\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java**: The main public consumer facade that delegates to either ClassicKafkaConsumer or AsyncKafkaConsumer based on group protocol configuration (KIP-848). This is the primary entry point for all consumer operations.\\n\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegate.java**: Internal interface extending the Consumer interface, providing methods for internal use (clientId(), metricsRegistry(), kafkaConsumerMetrics(), updateAssignmentMetadataIfNeeded()).\\n\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegateCreator.java**: Factory class that inspects ConsumerConfig.GROUP_PROTOCOL_CONFIG and creates either AsyncKafkaConsumer (for 'consumer' protocol) or ClassicKafkaConsumer (for legacy/classic protocol).\\n\\n**Legacy Group Protocol Implementation:**\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java**: Implements ConsumerDelegate<K, V> for the classic group protocol (pre-KIP 848). Contains synchronous implementation using ConsumerCoordinator for group coordination and offset management. This is the backward-compatible implementation.\\n\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerCoordinator.java**: Manages group coordination and offset commits for ClassicKafkaConsumer. Key offset management methods:\\n  - commitOffsetsSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>, Timer): Synchronously commits offsets\\n  - commitOffsetsAsync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>, OffsetCommitCallback): Asynchronously commits offsets\\n  - Tracks in-flight async commits and invokes callbacks upon completion\\n\\n**New Group Protocol Implementation:**\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java**: Implements ConsumerDelegate<K, V> for the new consumer group protocol (KIP-848). Uses event-based architecture with dedicated request managers for handling network I/O asynchronously.\\n\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java**: Manages offset commits in AsyncKafkaConsumer using an event-driven approach. Features:\\n  - Uses PendingRequests queue for managing commit requests\\n  - Supports both sync and async commits through events (SyncCommitEvent, AsyncCommitEvent)\\n  - Implements AutoCommitState for periodic automatic offset commits\\n  - Integrates with CoordinatorRequestManager for group coordination\\n\\n**Offset Management Infrastructure:**\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/OffsetFetcher.java**: Handles fetching committed offsets from brokers. Used by ClassicKafkaConsumer for offset initialization and recovery.\\n\\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/OffsetAndMetadata.java**: Data class representing an offset with associated metadata, used throughout both implementations for offset commit/fetch operations.\\n\\n### Key Behavioral Differences in Offset Management\\n\\n**ClassicKafkaConsumer (Legacy Group Protocol):**\\n1. **Synchronous Architecture**: All network operations are blocking, occurring in the application thread\\n2. **ConsumerCoordinator Managed**: Single coordinator handles both group membership and offset management\\n3. **Offset Commit Flow**: Direct API calls to commitSync() and commitAsync() trigger immediate offset commit requests\\n4. **Callback Model**: Uses OffsetCommitCallback for async completion notification\\n5. **Rebalance Handling**: Synchronous rebalance listeners invoked on application thread\\n\\n**AsyncKafkaConsumer (New Group Protocol - KIP-848):**\\n1. **Event-Driven Architecture**: Network operations use event-based, asynchronous model with background threads\\n2. **Separated Concerns**: CommitRequestManager handles offset commits separately from CoordinatorRequestManager (group coordination)\\n3. **Offset Commit Flow**: Commit requests are enqueued as events (SyncCommitEvent/AsyncCommitEvent) for background processing\\n4. **CompletableFuture Model**: Async operations return CompletableFuture instead of using callbacks\\n5. **Rebalance Handling**: Asynchronous rebalance listener invocation with proper event sequencing\\n\\n### Integration Points\\n\\n#### Camel Kafka Component (sg-evals/camel--1006f047)\\n\\nCamel integrates with the modern KafkaConsumer API through:\\n- **components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/KafkaConsumer.java**: Camel's consumer wrapper around org.apache.kafka.clients.consumer.Consumer interface\\n- **components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/KafkaFetchRecords.java**: Fetches records using the underlying Kafka consumer and manages offset state\\n- **components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/DefaultKafkaClientFactory.java**: Factory that instantiates org.apache.kafka.clients.consumer.KafkaConsumer\\n- **Commit Managers**: \\n  - **SyncCommitManager.java**: Performs synchronous offset commits via consumer.commitSync()\\n  - **AsyncCommitManager.java**: Performs asynchronous offset commits via consumer.commitAsync()\\n  - **CommitManagers.java**: Factory that selects the appropriate commit manager based on configuration\\n\\n#### Flink Kafka Connector (sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc)\\n\\n- **flink-python/pyflink/datastream/connectors/kafka.py**: FlinkKafkaConsumer is deprecated in favor of KafkaSource. This represents the legacy wrapper approach that has been superseded by modern source implementations.\\n\\n### Migration Path Summary\\n\\n1. **Old API (kafka.consumer.ConsumerConnector)**: Deprecated and removed in Kafka 4.0, used pre-KIP-848\\n2. **Current KafkaConsumer with ClassicKafkaConsumer**: Maintains backward compatibility with classic group protocol\\n3. **Modern AsyncKafkaConsumer**: Implements new KIP-848 protocol with event-driven architecture\\n4. **Consumer abstraction level**: All implementations use Consumer interface at abstraction boundary (as seen in Camel)\\n\\nThe migration preserves backward compatibility while enabling more efficient, event-driven consumer implementations through the delegation pattern, allowing applications to seamlessly upgrade to the new protocol without changing their code.\"\n}\n",
